Executive Summary with Lineage\n    34→\n    35→### Derivation\n    36→\n    37→This specification is the product of two independent analysis runs examining the same problem -- the quality gap between the legacy manual cleanup-audit prompts and the current automated `sc:cleanup-audit` v1. The two analysis sets were merged through a structured adversarial process:\n    38→\n    39→- **Set A** (single-agent, 2 documents): Gap analysis comparing old prompt outputs to new audit output, plus a vNext PRD with Pass 4 docs audit, known-issues registry, and output schema hardening. Average composite score: 7.70/10.\n    40→- **Set B** (multi-agent, 4 documents): 15 findings from 4-agent parallel analysis, 12 debated proposals, 5-dimension reflection/validation, and a v2 PRD with 5-phase architecture. Average composite score: 8.55/10.\n    41→- **Merge process**: Wave 1 (coverage matrix, strength rankings, flaw analysis, conflict register) identified 45 topics, 22 conflicts, and 43 flaws. Wave 2 (advocate debate, devil's advocate attack, synthesis judge verdicts) resolved all 22 conflicts: 14 Set B, 7 HYBRID, 0 Set A.\n    42→\n    43→### Decision Lineage Summary\n    44→\n    45→| Decision | Source | Reference |\n    46→|----------|--------|-----------|\n    47→| 5-phase architecture | Set B ss3, modified per Verdict C-01 | Phase 0 Profile + Phase 4 Consolidation bookend scanning |\n    48→| Two-tier classification | Set B ss4, modified per Verdict C-03 | 4 primary + qualifiers with INVESTIGATE:human-review-needed added |\n    49→| Default budget 500K | Set B ss6, increased per Verdict C-08 | Original 300K deemed insufficient by flaw analysis F-B-02 |\n    50→| Minimal docs in core flow | HYBRID per Verdict C-02 | Broken refs + temporal in Phase 3; full opt-in via --pass-docs | [Source: HYBRID C-02] |\n    70→\n    71→---\n    72→\n    73→## 2. Problem Statement\n    74→\n    75→### The Spec-Implementation Gap [Source: Set B ss2]\n    76→\n    77→The current `sc:cleanup-audit` v1 spec at `/config/.claude/commands/sc/cleanup-audit.md` already promises features that were never implemented. This is the single most important structural finding from the analysis -- identified by Set B's reflection validation (B3, Dimension 2) and rated CRITICAL:\n    78→\n    79→| Spec Promise | Implementation Status |\n    80→|-------------|---------------------|\n    81→| 5 categories: DELETE/CONSOLIDATE/MOVE/FLAG/KEEP | NOT IMPLEMENTED -- only DELETE/REVIEW/KEEP used |\n    82→| Coverage tracking: \"transparently report what was and was not audited\" | NOT IMPLEMENTED -- no coverage metrics |\n    83→| Checkpointing: \"resume-from-checkpoint on session interruption\" | NOT IMPLEMENTED -- no progress.json written |\n    84→| Evidence-gated classification: \"requiring grep proof for every recommendation\" | PARTIAL -- DELETE has evidence; KEEP has none |\n    85→| Spot-check validation: \"10%\" | NOT IMPLEMENTED -- no validation pass |\n    86→\n    87→**Root cause**: v1 scanners were generic (6 unnamed parallel scanners) with no structured output schema, no batch file assignments, and no inter-pass coordination. The architecture could not enforce the spec's requirements. [Source: Set B ss2]\n    88→\n    89→**v2 requirement**: All v1 spec promises MUST be implemented before any new features are added. This is Implementation Phase 0.\n    90→\n    91→### The Quantified Quality Gap [Source: Set B Finding 2]\n    92→\n    93→The v1 audit produced 12 per-file profiles out of 5,857 files -- a 99.8% miss rate. The legacy manual approach, using 27 targeted batch reports across 4 passes with human curation, produced 527+ profiles. While these numbers are not directly comparable (the manual approach involved 10-20 hours of human-guided work vs a single automated run) [Source: FLAW F-B-01], normalizing by effort still reveals a substantial gap in per-file analysis depth. The v2 spec targets budget-relative profile counts, not raw numbers.\n    94→\n    95→### The User-Facing Gap [Source: Set A ss1]\n    96→\n    97→From the user's perspective, the v1 output is \"often insightful at the repo level but less engineer-executable for documentation and for long-lived cleanup programs.\" Specifically:\n    98→\n    99→1. **No documentation quality assessment** -- the audit has \"near-zero signal about documentation correctness\" [Source: Set A ss1]\n   100→2. **No known-issues suppression** -- repeated audits rediscover the same 34+ known issues each time [Source: Set A ss4.4]\n   101→3. **Weak broken-reference reporting** -- format and systematic sweep are inadequate, especially for docs [Source: Set A ss1 Pass 1]\n   102→4. **No ARCHIVE-vs-DELETE guidance** for temporal documentation artifacts [Source: Set A ss1]\n   103→5. **Credential scanning produces wrong answers** -- real credentials in `.env.production` misidentified as template values [Source: Set B Finding 6]\n   104→\n   105→---\n   106→\n   107→## 3. Goals, Non-Goals, Target Users\n   108→\n   109→### Goals\n   110→\n   111→**Structural goals** (fix the foundation) [Source: Set B ss1]:\n   112→1. Enforce the existing v1 spec -- implement all unimplemented promises before adding new capabilities\n   113→2. Add structured batch decomposition -- domain-aware scanning with explicit file assignments\n   114→3. Require evidence for all classifications -- tiered evidence requirements based on file risk\n   115→4. Detect cross-boundary dead code -- dependency analysis after parallel scanning using static tools where available\n   116→5. Control costs -- hard budget ceiling with proportional phase allocation and graceful degradation\n   117→\n   118→**User-facing goals** (fill the output gaps) [Source: Set A ss2]:\n   119→- G1. Provide a minimal documentation audit (broken references + temporal artifact classification) in the core flow, with a full docs quality pass available via --pass-docs\n   120→- G2. Support a known-issues mechanism so repeated findings are suppressed with attribution rather than re-flagged each run\n   121→- G3. Harden output schemas so critical buckets (BROKEN_REFERENCES, ARCHIVE, FLAG, coverage accounting) are consistently emitted\n   122→- G4. Preserve the current system's strengths: evidence-backed triage, duplication matrices, conservative deletion\n   123→- G5. Maintain cost control: avoid unbounded analysis and keep outputs scannable\n   124→\n   125→### Non-Goals [Source: Set A ss2]\n   126→\n   127→- **N1**: This is not a \"cleanup executor.\" v2 remains read-only. No automated delete/move operations. [Source: Set A N1]\n   128→- **N2**: This is not a full semantic doc correctness checker. The docs audit focuses on structural correctness (paths, referenced files, ports, scripts), plus overlap detection and link integrity. [Source: Set A N2]\n   129→- **N3**: No attempt to eliminate human judgment; archive/delete decisions remain recommendations. [Source: Set A N3]\n   130→- **N4**: This is not a security audit substitute. Credential scanning provides basic pattern detection only. Users should use truffleHog/detect-secrets for comprehensive scanning. [Source: Set B ss5 Phase 1 disclaimer]\n   131→\n   132→### Target Users [Source: Set A ss3]\n   133→\n   134→| Persona | Need | Primary Use Case |\n   135→|---------|------|-----------------|\n   136→| **Repo maintainers** | Periodic audits to keep repo size, CI, and onboarding sane | U1: \"Run audit and get an action list I can execute immediately\" |\n   137→| **Onboarding authors** | Ensure docs don't point to dead scripts, wrong paths, or stale architectures | U3: \"Find broken doc links and stale release artifacts without reading the entire docs tree\" |\n   138→| **DevOps owners** | Track deploy/config drift and prevent \"competing systems sprawl\" | U2: \"Run audit weekly without re-discovering known issues\" |\n   139→\n   140→---\n   141→\n   142→## 4. Architecture\n   143→\n   144→### 5-Phase Execution Model [Source: Set B ss3, Verdict C-01]\n   145→\n   146→sc:cleanup-audit v2 is a 5-phase read-only repository audit. Phase 0 (Profile & Plan) and Phase 4 (Consolidation & Validation) bookend the core scanning phases, providing the infrastructure enforcement layer that was absent in v1.\n   147→\n   148→```\n   149→Phase 0: Profile & Plan (Haiku, 30-60s)\n   150→    |\n   151→    +-- Detect domains (infrastructure, source, assets, docs)\n   152→    +-- Classify files into risk tiers (1-4)\n   153→    +-- Generate batch manifest (JSON)\n   154→    +-- Run static analysis tools where available (madge, pydeps)  [Source: DA Attack 1, HYBRID C-10]\n   155→    +-- Auto-generate config if absent\n   156→    |\n   157→    v\n   158→Phase 1: Surface Scan (Haiku scanners, parallel)\n   159→    |\n   160→    +-- Domain-aware batches with explicit file lists\n   161→    +-- Classify: DELETE / KEEP / MODIFY / INVESTIGATE\n   162→    +-- Credential file scanning (read actual content)\n   163→    +-- Gitignore consistency check\n   164→    |\n   165→    v\n   166→Phase 2: Structural Audit (Sonnet analyzers, parallel)\n   167→    |\n   168→    +-- 8-field profiles for DELETE/INVESTIGATE candidates + Tier 1-2 KEEP\n   169→    +-- File-type-specific verification rules\n   170→    +-- Signal-triggered depth escalation\n   171→    +-- Full docs audit if --pass-docs activated  [Source: HYBRID C-02]\n   172→    |\n   173→    v\n   174→Phase 3: Cross-Reference Synthesis (Sonnet comparator)\n   175→    |\n   176→    +-- Build dependency graph using 3-tier detection  [Source: HYBRID C-10]\n   177→    +-- Detect cross-boundary dead code\n   178→    +-- Produce duplication matrices\n   179→    +-- Minimal docs audit: broken references + temporal classification  [Source: HYBRID C-02]\n   180→    +-- Resolve INVESTIGATE classifications\n   181→    +-- Post-hoc deduplication  [Source: Set B Proposal 10]\n   182→    |\n   183→    v\n   184→Phase 4: Consolidation & Validation (Sonnet)\n   185→    |\n   186→    +-- Consolidate all findings, deduplicate across phases\n   187→    +-- Spot-check 10% of classifications (consistency rate)\n   188→    +-- Generate coverage report per tier\n   189→    +-- Directory-level assessment blocks for 50+ file dirs  [Source: Set A unique #3]\n   190→    +-- Write FINAL-REPORT.md\n   191→    |\n   192→    v\n   193→Output: .claude-audit/run-{timestamp}/\n   194→```\n   195→\n   196→### Subagent System [Source: Set B ss3, HYBRID C-06]\n   197→\n   198→**Target architecture** is Set B's 6-agent system. **Implementation starts** with Set A's conservative approach (reuse existing scanners for Phase 0-1), adding specialized agents incrementally in Phase 2+. [Source: HYBRID C-06]\n   199→\n   200→| Agent | Model | Role | Phase |\n   201→|-------|-------|------|-------|\n   202→| **audit-profiler** | Haiku | Repository profiling, domain detection, tier assignment, static tool orchestration | 0 |\n   203→| **audit-scanner** | Haiku | Surface classification with evidence (simplified schema) | 1 |\n   204→| **audit-analyzer** | Sonnet | Deep structural analysis with 8-field profiles | 2 |\n   205→| **audit-comparator** | Sonnet | Cross-reference synthesis, dependency graphs | 3 |\n   206→| **audit-consolidator** | Sonnet | Report consolidation, deduplication, directory assessment | 4 |\n   207→| **audit-validator** | Sonnet | Spot-check re-verification (10% sample) | 4 |\n   208→\n   209→**Schema split rationale** [Source: FLAW F-B-06]: The Phase 1 Haiku schema is simplified to essential fields only (path, classification, primary_action, qualifier, confidence, evidence_text). Complex structured fields (import_references arrays, export_targets arrays, external_dependencies) move to Phase 2 Sonnet analyzers. This reduces Haiku malformation risk while preserving the dependency graph data pipeline.\n   210→\n   211→### Standardized Scanner Output Schema [Source: Set B ss3, scored 9.3 -- highest in either set]\n   212→\n   213→**Phase 1 Schema (Haiku -- simplified):**\n   214→\n   215→```json\n   216→{\n   217→  \"scanner_id\": \"string\",\n   218→  \"domain\": \"string\",\n   219→  \"batch_id\": \"string\",\n   220→  \"files_assigned\": \"integer\",\n   221→  \"files_examined\": \"integer\",\n   222→  \"files\": [{\n   223→    \"path\": \"string\",\n   224→    \"risk_tier\": \"1|2|3|4\",\n   225→    \"classification\": {\n   226→      \"primary\": \"DELETE|KEEP|MODIFY|INVESTIGATE\",\n   227→      \"qualifier\": \"string\",\n   228→      \"confidence\": \"0.0-1.0\"\n   229→    },\n   230→    \"evidence_text\": \"string (free-text summary of evidence: grep commands run, results, rationale)\",\n   231→    \"credential_scan\": \"null|{has_real_credentials: bool, disclaimer: string}\"\n   232→  }]\n   233→}\n   234→```\n   235→\n   236→**Phase 2 Schema (Sonnet -- full 8-field profile):**\n   237→\n   238→```json\n   239→{\n   240→  \"file_path\": \"string\",\n   241→  \"classification\": \"Primary:Qualifier\",\n   242→  \"size_bytes\": \"integer\",\n   243→  \"evidence\": {\n   244→    \"import_references\": [\"list of files that import/reference this file\"],\n   245→    \"grep_command\": \"exact grep command used\",\n   246→    \"grep_result_count\": \"integer\",\n   247→    \"last_commit_date\": \"ISO date\",\n   248→    \"last_commit_author\": \"string\",\n   249→    \"test_file_exists\": \"boolean\",\n   250→    \"dynamic_import_check\": \"none_found|possible_dynamic:[pattern]\"\n   251→  },\n   252→  \"risk_tier\": \"1-4\",\n   253→  \"rationale\": \"2-3 sentence explanation\",\n   254→  \"confidence\": \"0.0-1.0\",\n   255→  \"related_files\": [\"files that should be considered together\"]\n   256→}\n   257→```\n   258→\n   259→Note: The `test_coverage` field from Set B's original schema is replaced with `test_file_exists` (a boolean checking whether a corresponding test file exists), because determining actual test coverage requires running tests with instrumentation, which is infeasible in this context. [Source: FLAW F-B-21]\n   260→\n   261→**Schema validation**: Scanners that produce output not conforming to the schema trigger a validation error. The orchestrator retries the batch once, then marks it as FAILED in the coverage manifest. [Source: Set B ss3]\n   262→\n   263→### The Hybrid Architecture: Static Tools + LLM Judgment [Source: DA Attack 1, HYBRID C-10]\n   264→\n   265→The devil's advocate analysis identified the single largest architectural blind spot in both original analysis sets: neither proposed combining static analysis tools with LLM judgment. This unified spec addresses that gap directly.\n   266→\n   267→**Principle**: Ground truth must come from deterministic tools where possible. LLMs provide judgment, classification, and reporting -- not data gathering. [Source: DA Guard Rail 1]\n   268→\n   269→**Implementation**: Phase 0 runs available static analysis tools and feeds their output into the scanning pipeline:\n   270→\n   271→| Tool | Language | Purpose | Confidence |\n   272→|------|----------|---------|------------|\n   273→| `madge --orphans` | JS/TS | Orphan file detection | Tier A (high) |\n   274→| `pydeps` | Python | Dependency graph | Tier A (high) |\n   275→| `ts-prune` | TypeScript | Unused exports | Tier A (high) |\n   276→| `cargo-deps` | Rust | Dependency graph | Tier A (high) |\n   277→| `grep -rL` patterns | Any | Reference counting | Tier B (medium) |\n   278→| `git log --diff-filter=A` | Any | File creation dates | Tier A (high) |\n   279→| LLM inference from file reading | Any | Relationship inference | Tier C (low) |\n   280→\n   281→Static tool availability is detected in Phase 0. If a tool is not installed, the system falls back to the next tier. All dependency graph edges carry a confidence tier label (A/B/C). [Source: HYBRID C-10]\n   282→\n   283→---\n   284→\n   285→## 5. Unified Classification System [Source: Set B ss4, Verdict C-03]\n   286→\n   287→### Two-Tier System\n   288→\n   289→**Primary Action** (what to do):\n   290→- `DELETE` -- Remove the file\n   291→- `KEEP` -- No action needed\n   292→- `MODIFY` -- Keep but change something\n   293→- `INVESTIGATE` -- Insufficient evidence for automated classification; requires human input\n   294→\n   295→**Secondary Qualifier** (specifics):\n   296→\n   297→| Primary | Qualifier | Meaning |\n   298→|---------|-----------|---------|\n   299→| DELETE | `standard` | Safe to delete, zero references confirmed |\n   300→| DELETE | `archive-first` | Delete but preserve in archive (historically valuable). Report must include suggested destination path. [Source: Set A C-09 requirement] |\n   301→| KEEP | `verified` | Evidence confirms active use (Tier 1-2 evidence) |\n   302→| KEEP | `unverified` | No evidence checked (Tier 3-4 pattern match only) |\n   303→| KEEP | `monitor` | Active but shows warning signals (stale, low usage) |\n   304→| MODIFY | `consolidate-with:[target]` | Merge with another file |\n   305→| MODIFY | `fix-references` | Has broken references that need repair |\n   306→| MODIFY | `update-content` | Content is outdated or incorrect |\n   307→| MODIFY | `move-to:[destination]` | Should be relocated |\n   308→| MODIFY | `flag:[issue]` | Has specific issue needing attention (e.g., flag:gitignore-inconsistency) |\n   309→| INVESTIGATE | `cross-boundary` | Referenced across domain boundaries, unclear ownership |\n   310→| INVESTIGATE | `insufficient-evidence` | Evidence gathering failed or was inconclusive |\n   311→| INVESTIGATE | `dynamic-import` | May be loaded via dynamic import/require patterns |\n   312→| INVESTIGATE | `human-review-needed` | Genuinely ambiguous file requiring human judgment (not an evidence failure) [Source: FLAW F-B-19 mitigation] |\n   313→\n   314→**INVESTIGATE cap**: If INVESTIGATE exceeds 15% of examined files, trigger a re-analysis pass on those files with elevated budget. This prevents INVESTIGATE from becoming a dumping ground for lazy classification. [Source: FLAW F-B-11 mitigation, Verdict C-03]\n   315→\n   316→### Backward Compatibility Mapping [Source: Set B ss4]\n   317→\n   318→| v1 Category | v2 Mapping | Notes |\n   319→|-------------|-----------|-------|\n   320→| DELETE | DELETE:standard | Direct mapping |"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01CThaKtCCJHcWWksNFLojcM","session_id":"e849ddf0-0b85-4b2a-a2a9-f181c22e7a7b","uuid":"e66c7088-9a6e-49e0-bfe9-8b1e80261c18"}

Code block conventions: unclosed fenced code blocks.\n    \"\"\"\n    issues: list[StyleIssue] = []\n    lines = content.splitlines()\n\n    h1_count = 0\n    last_heading_level = 0\n    in_code_block = False\n    code_block_start = 0\n\n    for i, line in enumerate(lines, start=1):\n        # Track code blocks\n        if line.strip().startswith(\"```\"):\n            if in_code_block:\n                in_code_block = False\n            else:\n                in_code_block = True\n                code_block_start = i\n            continue\n\n        if in_code_block:\n            continue\n\n        # Heading checks\n        hm = _HEADING_PATTERN.match(line)\n        if hm:\n            level = len(hm.group(1))\n            if level == 1:\n                h1_count += 1\n                if h1_count > 1:\n                    issues.append(StyleIssue(\n                        file_path=file_path,\n                        line_number=i,\n                        issue_type=\"heading_hierarchy\",\n                        description=\"Multiple H1 headings\",\n                    ))\n            if last_heading_level > 0 and level > last_heading_level + 1:\n                issues.append(StyleIssue(\n                    file_path=file_path,\n                    line_number=i,\n                    issue_type=\"heading_hierarchy\",\n                    description=f\"Heading level skipped: H{last_heading_level} -> H{level}\",\n                ))\n            last_heading_level = level\n\n        # Bare URL check (URLs not inside markdown link syntax or code)\n        bare_urls = re.findall(r\"(?<!\\()(https?://\\S+)(?!\\))\", line)\n        for url in bare_urls:\n            # Skip if inside a markdown link [text](url)\n            if f\"]({url})\" in line:\n                continue\n            issues.append(StyleIssue(\n                file_path=file_path,\n                line_number=i,\n                issue_type=\"link_format\",\n                description=f\"Bare URL: {url}\",\n            ))\n\n    # Unclosed code block\n    if in_code_block:\n        issues.append(StyleIssue(\n            file_path=file_path,\n            line_number=code_block_start,\n            issue_type=\"code_block_convention\",\n            description=\"Unclosed fenced code block\",\n        ))\n\n    return issues\n\n\ndef full_docs_audit(\n    doc_files: dict[str, str],\n    known_files: set[str],\n    code_files: set[str] | None = None,\n    exported_symbols: dict[str, list[str]] | None = None,\n    last_modified: dict[str, str] | None = None,\n    threshold_days: int = 365,\n    current_date: datetime | None = None,\n) -> FullDocsAuditResult:\n    \"\"\"Run full 5-section docs audit (--pass-docs).\n\n    Args:\n        doc_files: Mapping of doc_file_path -> content.\n        known_files: All known file paths.\n        code_files: Set of code file paths (for orphan detection).\n        exported_symbols: Mapping source_file -> exported symbol names.\n        last_modified: Mapping file_path -> ISO date.\n        threshold_days: Staleness threshold in days.\n        current_date: Current date for staleness check.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Sections 1 & 2: reuse minimal audit\n    minimal = audit_docs(\n        doc_files, known_files, last_modified, threshold_days, current_date,\n    )\n\n    # Section 3: coverage gaps\n    coverage_gaps = detect_coverage_gaps(\n        exported_symbols or {}, doc_files,\n    )\n\n    # Section 4: orphaned docs\n    orphaned = detect_orphaned_docs(doc_files, code_files or set())\n\n    # Section 5: style issues\n    style_issues: list[StyleIssue] = []\n    for file_path, content in doc_files.items():\n        style_issues.extend(check_style_issues(file_path, content))\n\n    return FullDocsAuditResult(\n        broken_links=minimal.broken_links,\n        stale_docs=minimal.stale_docs,\n        coverage_gaps=coverage_gaps,\n        orphaned_docs=orphaned,\n        style_issues=style_issues,\n    )\n","numLines":469,"startLine":1,"totalLines":469}}}

\"\"\"Build a dependency graph where dead files have no inbound edges.\"\"\"\n    graph = DependencyGraph()\n    dead = dead_files or set()\n    live = [f for f in files if f not in dead and f.endswith(\".py\")]\n\n    # Connect live files in a chain\n    for i in range(1, len(live)):\n        edge = DependencyEdge(\n            source=live[i - 1],\n            target=live[i],\n imports them)\n    for df in dead:\n        if live:\n            edge = DependencyEdge(\n                source=df,\n                target=live[0],\n                tier=EdgeTier.TIER_A,\n        profile = profile_file(f, size_bytes=100, line_count=50)\n            assert isinstance(profile, FileProfile)\n\n\nclass TestBenchmarkMediumRepo:\n    \"\"\"Benchmark on medium repo (50-500      tracker = CoverageTracker(total_files_scanned=len(files))\n        for f in files[:100]:\n            result = ClassificationResult(\n                file_path=f,\n artifact = tracker.emit()\n        assert artifact.total_files_classified >= 100\n\n\nclass TestBenchmarkDeadCodeRepo:\n    \"\"\"Benchmark on known-dead-code repo.\"\"\"\n\n    def test_dead_code_detection_accuracy(self):\n        all_files, expected_dead = _dead_code_repo()\n        graph = _build_graph_for_files(all_files, dead_files=expected_dead)\n        analyses =    )\n\n    def test_dead_code_no_false_positives_on_live(self):\n        all_files, expected_dead = _dead_code_repo()\n        graph = _build_graph_for_files(all_files, dead_files=expected_dead)\n        analyses = _build_file_analyses(all_files)\n\n        report = detect_dead_code(\n            file_analyses=analyses,\n            dependency_graph=graph,\n        )\n\n        detected_files = Cache entries are keyed by content hash within the in-memory instance, not shared across runs.\n3. **Registry isolation**: Known-issues registries are loaded from and saved to per-run paths.\n4. **Output isolation**: Batch decomposition is deterministic — same inputs produce same outputs, meaning concurrent runs on identical input produce identical (not conflicting) results.\n\n## Verification Approach\n\n- **Thread safety**: Two threads write checkpoints simultaneously to separate directories; both read back correctly with no corruption.\n- **Cache independence**: Two separate `ResultCache` instances store different results for the same content hash without cross-contamination.\n- **Registry independence**: Two separate registry files on different paths are loaded/saved independently.\n- **Determinism**: Same file list + batch size → identical batch IDs, ensuring concurrent-vs-sequential equivalence.\n\n## Test File\n- `tests/audit/test_concurrent_isolation.py` — 8 tests across 4 test classes\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1420,"cache_read_input_tokens":147651,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":1420,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e849ddf0-0b85-4b2a-a2a9-f181c22e7a7b","uuid":"22940a36-893f-4beb-90e4-f375446156e8"}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-6","id":"msg_01M6j9AjkmZ5iY9yZTcVLRmr","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_019mMyt6LjXf2vRawfHYXhJE","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/config/workspace/SuperClaude_Framework/.dev/releases/current/cleanup-audit-v2-UNIFIED-SPEC/tasklist/artifacts/D-0047/spec.md","content":"# D-0047 Spec: Non-Determinism Sources and Known Limitations\n\n## Task Reference\n- Task: T05.08\n- Roadmap Item: R-047\n- AC: AC6 (quality extension)\n\n## Limitations Section Format\n\nThe limitations section is placed in the final report between validation results and appendix.\n\n## Identified Non-Determinism Sources\n\n### 1. LLM Classification Variance\n\n**Source**: When the audit delegates classification decisions to an LLM (e.g., for ambiguous INVESTIGATE candidates), the output can vary between runs even with identical input.\n\n**Impact**: Classification of borderline files may differ between runs by 1-2 action categories. This primarily affects Tier-2 and Tier-3 files where confidence is lower.\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Evidence-gated decisions: DELETE requires grep evidence with 0 references\n- Confidence thresholds: findings below threshold are flagged as INVESTIGATE rather than acted upon\n- Anti-lazy guard: detects suspiciously uniform batches (>90% same classification) that may indicate lazy LLM responses\n- Spot-check validation: 10% stratified sample re-classification measures self-consistency\n\n### 2. Git History Dependency\n\n**Source**: Staleness checks, file age computation, and churn metrics depend on git history depth. Shallow clones or repos with squashed history may produce different profiling results.\n\n**Impact**: Files may be incorrectly assessed as \"old\" or \"low churn\" if git history is truncated. This affects profiling accuracy for risk tier assignment.\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Staleness checks use `git log --follow` where available\n- Missing git dates are treated as \"unknown\" rather than defaulting\n- Profile generator documents when git data is unavailable\n- Budget caveat notes explicitly state that results depend on available git history\n\n### 3. Dynamic Import Detection Limits\n\n**Source**: Static analysis cannot resolve dynamic imports (`importlib.import_module`, `__import__`, `getattr` on modules). Files that are only imported dynamically may be falsely classified as dead code.\n\n**Impact**: False positive DELETE recommendations for files consumed exclusively through dynamic import patterns. This is a fundamental limitation of static analysis.\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Dynamic import pattern scanner detects `importlib`, `__import__`, and `getattr` patterns\n- Files with detected dynamic import consumption receive KEEP:monitor classification (never DELETE)\n- Exclusion list for known framework hooks (pytest fixtures, Django migrations, etc.)\n- Documentation warns that dynamic import consumers should be verified manually\n\n### 4. Tier-C Inference Confidence\n\n**Source**: Tier-C dependency edges (co-occurrence inference) are heuristic — they detect files that frequently appear together in git commits but may not have actual import relationships.\n\n**Impact**: Low-confidence dependency edges may create false relationships, causing some dead code to be missed (false negatives) or non-dead code to appear referenced (reducing detection rate).\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Tier-C edges are weighted at 40% vs Tier-A's 100%\n- Dead code detection primarily relies on Tier-A (static imports) and Tier-B (grep references)\n- Tier-C evidence is labeled in reports to distinguish from stronger evidence types\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3558,"cache_read_input_tokens":148158,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":3558,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":5,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e849ddf0-0b85-4b2a-a2a9-f181c22e7a7b","uuid":"68569b37-f376-46ac-933e-31b3975e0845"}

LLM Classification Variance\n\n**Source**: When the audit delegates classification decisions to an LLM (e.g., for ambiguous INVESTIGATE candidates), the output can vary between runs even with identical input.\n\n**Impact**: Classification of borderline files may differ between runs by 1-2 action categories. This primarily affects Tier-2 and Tier-3 files where confidence is lower.\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Evidence-gated decisions: DELETE requires grep evidence with 0 references\n- Confidence thresholds: findings below threshold are flagged as INVESTIGATE rather than acted upon\n- Anti-lazy guard: detects suspiciously uniform batches (>90% same classification) that may indicate lazy LLM responses\n- Spot-check validation: 10% stratified sample re-classification measures self-consistency\n\n### 2. Git History Dependency\n\n**Source**: Staleness checks, file age computation, and churn metrics depend on git history depth. Shallow clones or repos with squashed history may produce different profiling results.\n\n**Impact**: Files may be incorrectly assessed as \"old\" or \"low churn\" if git history is truncated. This affects profiling accuracy for risk tier assignment.\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Staleness checks use `git log --follow` where available\n- Missing git dates are treated as \"unknown\" rather than defaulting\n- Profile generator documents when git data is unavailable\n- Budget caveat notes explicitly state that results depend on available git history\n\n### 3. Dynamic Import Detection Limits\n\n**Source**: Static analysis cannot resolve dynamic imports (`importlib.import_module`, `__import__`, `getattr` on modules). Files that are only imported dynamically may be falsely classified as dead code.\n\n**Impact**: False positive DELETE recommendations for files consumed exclusively through dynamic import patterns. This is a fundamental limitation of static analysis.\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Dynamic import pattern scanner detects `importlib`, `__import__`, and `getattr` patterns\n- Files with detected dynamic import consumption receive KEEP:monitor classification (never DELETE)\n- Exclusion list for known framework hooks (pytest fixtures, Django migrations, etc.)\n- Documentation warns that dynamic import consumers should be verified manually\n\n### 4. Tier-C Inference Confidence\n\n**Source**: Tier-C dependency edges (co-occurrence inference) are heuristic — they detect files that frequently appear together in git commits but may not have actual import relationships.\n\n**Impact**: Low-confidence dependency edges may create false relationships, causing some dead code to be missed (false negatives) or non-dead code to appear referenced (reducing detection rate).\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Tier-C edges are weighted at 40% vs Tier-A's 100%\n- Dead code detection primarily relies on Tier-A (static imports) and Tier-B (grep references)\n- Tier-C evidence is labeled in reports to distinguish from stronger evidence types\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
